<div id="review_1778596909" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1778596909" />
    <a title="RedemptionDenied" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55677020-redemptiondenied"><img alt="RedemptionDenied" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1778596909?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="RedemptionDenied" class="user" itemprop="url" name="RedemptionDenied" href="/user/show/55677020-redemptiondenied">RedemptionDenied</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781455561780" href="/book/show/26245850-before-the-fall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=review-of-another-edition">review-of-another-edition</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55677020-redemptiondenied?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1778596909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6828141352016907367">When I bought this a few months back - I didn't know it was from the creator/writer of the TV series' Fargo, which would explain the humour throughout the book.<br/><br/>A private aircraft departs from Martha's Vineyard to New York in foggy conditions; with eight passenger's and three crew members on-board the Ospray 700 SL, which was manufactured in Kansas. The flight under normal conditions should take about twenty nine minutes but, sixteen minutes into the flight, the aircraft crashes into the Atlantic</span>
  <span id="freeText6828141352016907367" style="display:none">When I bought this a few months back - I didn't know it was from the creator/writer of the TV series' Fargo, which would explain the humour throughout the book.<br /><br />A private aircraft departs from Martha's Vineyard to New York in foggy conditions; with eight passenger's and three crew members on-board the Ospray 700 SL, which was manufactured in Kansas. The flight under normal conditions should take about twenty nine minutes but, sixteen minutes into the flight, the aircraft crashes into the Atlantic - and there are only two survivors: Scott Burrough's, a painter, and JJ, the four-year-old son of David Bateman, who is a wealthy and powerful media mogul (President) - of the twenty four hour news network - ALC News.<br /><br />Scott was invited onto the flight by David Bateman's wife, Maggie, who saw him at the Farmers Market - she also saw her friend, Sarah Kipling, and she got an invite, too. The plane nearly left without him but, he just about made it as the door was closing, so that was stroke of luck. Now Scott is fighting for his life in the Atlantic Ocean with a four-year-old boy and he has no idea which way to swim in order to reach land plus, he has a dislocated shoulder. He hazards a guess, then realises he was on the verge of going in the wrong direction, which would have taken him further away from land. Luckily, there was a brief parting in the fog; so he was able to navigate by the constellations. Even luckier; when Scott was six, he was with his family watching a man, Jack Lahanne, swim from Alcatraz Island to the mainland pulling a thousand pound boat whilst his wrists were tied together - which gave Scott the inspiration to join the swim team. Some of the descriptions of Lahanne were quite funny.<br /><br />The story alternates between the aftermath of the crash and the back-stories of those aboard the fatal flight. We also have the backstories of some of the people affected by the tragedy. I would have liked to have had some back-story of Special Agent Walter. O'Brien of the FBI - as that may have given some insight as to why he was such an asshole. Actually, most of the characters had flaws, but none of them were of the same calibre as O'brien. He was in a league of his own. Must have taken him years of practice perfecting the art. So basically, this is a book of two mysteries; one being a plane crash, the other.....and only one them gets solved.<br /><br />Anyway, Scott eventually reaches land, and he's a hero to some, and a person of interest to others. He tries to keep a low profile but, that can only go on for so long. Every opportunity he gets he keeps making bad decisions, and as an artist it doesn't help that he paints disasters: train wrecks, tornados, plane crashes, etcetera, so he comes under suspicion. Why did he and the boy survive, and none of the other passengers? One of the passengers, Ben Kipling, was on the verge of being indicted for laundering money, so did that have something to do with the crash? Was it an act of terrorism? Pilot error? Or mechanical failure? One things for sure: Scott wasn't prepared for the media circus that follows.<br /><br />I had a few issues with some of the dialogue: incomplete sentences, where characters would say something like - 'I mean - well, maybe - no, hang on, what I meant to say was,' etcetera. And it was like that with the majority of the cast. As if they were course correcting everything they said or, thinking better of saying certain things at the last possible moment. So the writing style took a bit of getting used to. <br /><br />In summation: I really enjoyed the book, it was interesting and funny. Most of the cast were unlikable (not just O'Brien) - although, their back-stories were intriguing. I'll have to check out other novels by the author, sometime.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6828141352016907367" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1568717179" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1568717179" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1568717179?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781455561780" href="/book/show/26245850-before-the-fall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5872506-larry-h?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1568717179" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14908592117203755439">Full disclosure: I received an advance copy of this book from NetGalley in exchange for an unbiased review. Many thanks to NetGalley and Grand Central Publishing for making it available!<br/><br/>It's an evening in late August, a little foggy but otherwise uneventful. On Martha's Vineyard, the private plane belonging to David Bateman, the power behind one of the country's major cable news networks, is scheduled to take off and head back to New York. David and his wife Maggie, and their two young children,</span>
  <span id="freeText14908592117203755439" style="display:none">Full disclosure: I received an advance copy of this book from NetGalley in exchange for an unbiased review. Many thanks to NetGalley and Grand Central Publishing for making it available!<br /><br />It's an evening in late August, a little foggy but otherwise uneventful. On Martha's Vineyard, the private plane belonging to David Bateman, the power behind one of the country's major cable news networks, is scheduled to take off and head back to New York. David and his wife Maggie, and their two young children, nine-year-old Rachel and four-year-old JJ, are ready to head home, and their friends Sarah and Ben Kipling are joining them on the flight. Maggie has also invited Scott Burroughs, a painter that she has befriended on their many visits to the Vineyard.<br /><br />Scott arrives late, just as the plane was preparing to take off, so he tries to relax. There's music playing, and David and Ben are watching the Boston Red Sox game. Small talk is exchanged, and the flight attendant offers everyone a beverage. And then, inexplicably, 16 minutes after takeoff, the plane plunges into the ocean.<br /><br />Scott regains consciousness in the ocean and begins to realize what has happened. As he tries to find other survivors of the crash, he hears the cries of JJ, apparently the only other person left alive. Despite a shoulder injury, Scott, once a championship swimmer inspired by the legendary Jack LaLanne's swim from Alcatraz when Scott was a boy, swims with JJ nearly 10 miles to shore.<br /><br />As the authorities try to figure out what caused the crash, details are uncovered and theories begin to emerge. Was the plane brought down by someone determined to may David pay for his network's manipulating of popular opinion via the news it broadcasts? Were there other reasons for sabotage, perhaps related to one of the other passengers on board? Were the flight crew trustworthy?<br /><br />Of course, the person in the most blinding spotlight is Scott. While his heroism is heralded, it's also questioned, suspected. How did he wind up on the plane that night? What was his relationship with Maggie? How is he the only adult survivor from a plane full of important people? The media circles, leaving no stone unturned, questioning everything in his past, even the pictures he has painted. And as Scott reaches out to JJ given the bond they shared, there are some suspecting nefarious elements there, too.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Before the Fall</i>
</b> is a book that doesn't know what it wants to be. Is it a meditation on the fragility of life, the simplicity of luck, and the unconscious act of a hero? Is it a look at how quickly one's life can change, and the beauty of a simple bond between a man and a young child? Is it a portrait of our media-obsessed society, where in an effort to be first to break a story, the media broadcasts what it knows and then makes up what it doesn't, crafting facts to fit the theories they want to espouse? Or is it a thriller, as the authorities (of course, not without the usual pissing match between branches of the government) try to figure out what really did happen on the plane that night?<br /><br />Noah Hawley tries to make this book all of those things, which means it doesn't quite succeed on any of those fronts. It is beautifully written, and Scott is a fascinating character. If the book had concentrated on him and his life following the crash, and how JJ and those around him dealt with the aftermath, I think this would have been stronger and more appealing, at least for me. But the book gets bogged down in looking at the lives of each of the other passengers and crew on board that night, and what brought them to that moment, and then the zealous media coverage of the crash and the suspicions being levied against Scott (particularly by a corrupt anchor on David's network), and it really frustrated me.<br /><br />Since Hawley is the executive producer, writer, and showrunner for the television series <b>
  <i>Fargo</i>
</b>, this book is getting a lot of attention, and is even being hyped as "the thriller of the year." I'd nominate several other books I've read so far this year for that honor (particularly Gregg Hurwitz's <b>
  <i>Orphan X</i>
</b>), but despite the fact I think <b>
  <i>Before the Fall</i>
</b> suffered from a bit of an identity crisis, it's definitely a worthwhile, compelling read. <br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com">http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blo...</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14908592117203755439" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1672756939?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelli" href="/user/show/4146551-kelli">Kelli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4146551-kelli?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1672756939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18216252774435761957">I read much of this and listened to some of it on audio. To me it felt very much like a screenplay. I kept thinking of Lost, more because of the backstories than the plane crash. All tell and no show, I didn't find this overly compelling and I found the segments with the "newscaster" very realistic but exhausting. 3 stars.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1649242875" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1649242875" />
    <a title="Diane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/279256-diane"><img alt="Diane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1497365060p2/279256.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1649242875?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane" href="/user/show/279256-diane">Diane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781455561780" href="/book/show/26245850-before-the-fall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/279256-diane?shelf=mysteries-thrillers">mysteries-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/279256-diane?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1649242875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10772794178755020661">The first 50 pages of this book were FANTASTIC. Seriously thrilling stuff.<br/><br/>But after that great first section, it was a mixed bag. <br/><br/><i>Before the Fall</i> is the story of a private plane that crashed in the ocean after leaving Martha's Vineyard. Who was on the plane? Why were they there? What caused the plane to crash? What happens to the survivors?<br/><br/>If you ever saw the show "Lost," which also featured a plane crash, the structure of this novel reminded me of those episodes, in that the book jumps back and</span>
  <span id="freeText10772794178755020661" style="display:none">The first 50 pages of this book were FANTASTIC. Seriously thrilling stuff.<br /><br />But after that great first section, it was a mixed bag. <br /><br /><i>Before the Fall</i> is the story of a private plane that crashed in the ocean after leaving Martha's Vineyard. Who was on the plane? Why were they there? What caused the plane to crash? What happens to the survivors?<br /><br />If you ever saw the show "Lost," which also featured a plane crash, the structure of this novel reminded me of those episodes, in that the book jumps back and forth between current events and each character's backstory. The author, Noah Hawley, also writes for TV, so it's fitting that his novel reminded me of a TV show. At times this technique worked great, and at other times, it was tedious. (Hey, that's also true of Lost!)<br /><br />My favorite character in the book was Scott, one of only two people to survive the crash. (That's not a spoiler. You learn this in the first few pages.) I loved Scott's backstory about how he became a swimmer, which helped him survive in the ocean. Scott is also a painter, and he was a surprise guest on the plane that day. After the crash, the media decided Scott was suspicious and he was hounded by the press, and also questioned by investigators. <br /><br />Unfortunately, there were a lot of characters in the book who were unlikeable, including a Roger-Ailes-type TV executive, and a Bill-O'Reilly-type TV host, which was partly why it took me so long to finish this book. I got stalled because I disliked those characters so much, and their storylines took up a significant chunk of the novel. To be frank, I hate 24-hour news channels, especially ones whose name rhymes with Schmox News. So reading a novel that features huge sections about Schmox-News-esque figures wasn't fun or delightful — it was actually painful. But I have to give some credit to Hawley here, it was so difficult to read those parts because his story rang true. The plot points in the novel could have come from real life, and that mirror image of our media culture is disturbing.<br /><br />At this point you might be wondering why I rated this book 4 stars, considering how frustrated I got with it. Well, the thing is, it's still a good story, and it's a decent thriller. Mostly I enjoyed the book while I was reading, and there was some satisfaction in how the story turned out.<br /><br />Hawley does have one writing quirk I wish he would fix in future works: often when a character is asked a question, Hawley wrote, "Scott thinks about this." Or, "Scott thought about that." This phrase happened so frequently that I couldn't believe an editor didn't catch it. I listened to most of this book on audio, and that reaction really stood out. Maybe it's not as noticeable in print.<br /><br />So, bottom line, would you recommend this novel? Diane thinks about this. Diane looks at you, wonders if you're a more laidback reader than she is. Finally, she says, "Definitely."<br /><br /><b>Favorite Quotes</b><br />"Everyone has their path. The choices they've made. How any two people end up in the same place at the same time is a mystery. You get on an elevator with a dozen strangers. You ride a bus, wait in line for the bathroom. It happens every day. To try to predict the places we'll go and the people we'll meet would be pointless."<br /><br />"Floating in the North Atlantic, Scott realizes that he has never been more clear about who he is, his purpose. It's so obvious. He was put on this earth to conquer this ocean, to save this boy."<br /><br />"It is the job of the human brain to assemble all the input of our world — sighs, sounds, smells — into a coherent narrative. This is what memory is, a carefully calibrated story that we make up about our past. But what happens when those details crumble? ... What happens when your life can't be translated into a linear narrative?"</span>
  <a data-text-id="10772794178755020661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1679942849" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1679942849" />
    <a title="Robin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36555254-robin"><img alt="Robin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536187488p2/36555254.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1679942849?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin" href="/user/show/36555254-robin">Robin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781455562473" href="/book/show/31933278-before-the-fall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36555254-robin?shelf=american">american</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1679942849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3014626217933837632">I'm a little late to this party, as this was one of 2016's "it" thrillers. This is written by Noah Hawley, who in addition to writing four other novels, is also an award winning television screenwriter, and wrote and produced the awesome tv series <i>Fargo</i>. <br/><br/>As is quite evident by the book's cover, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26245850.Before_the_Fall' title='Before the Fall by Noah Hawley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Before the Fall</a> tells the mysterious story of a plane crash, in a private jet on its way to New York over the Atlantic ocean. Why did the plane crash? Was it a conspiracy? Does it have to do with one of t</span>
  <span id="freeText3014626217933837632" style="display:none">I'm a little late to this party, as this was one of 2016's "it" thrillers. This is written by Noah Hawley, who in addition to writing four other novels, is also an award winning television screenwriter, and wrote and produced the awesome tv series <i>Fargo</i>. <br /><br />As is quite evident by the book's cover, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26245850.Before_the_Fall" title="Before the Fall by Noah Hawley" rel="nofollow noopener">Before the Fall</a> tells the mysterious story of a plane crash, in a private jet on its way to New York over the Atlantic ocean. Why did the plane crash? Was it a conspiracy? Does it have to do with one of the 11 people on board, one of which was set to be jailed for laundering "bad" money, another the owner of a news station whose anchor was tapping phones to get the edge on the stories he covered. Not much is known, except a floundering painter and ex-alcoholic, Scott, survives, along with a four year old boy who he rescues in a bone chilling exertion.<br /><br />As he unfolds the keys to the mystery, Hawley introduces us, one by one, to each person on the private jet, giving us enough to see their individuality and the path that leads them to the plane. <br /><br />At first glance, this is a closed door mystery, an old fashioned whodunit. But it is more than that. It's a criticism of the media, the black and white way people are either demonized or made into heroes, the way things are oversimplified in order to make headlines, and the amoral methods used to get the juiciest details. People cease to be seen as human beings - humanity is sucked out for the sake of sensationalism.<br /><br />It also takes a hard look at money, its trappings, what it does to some people who have it or want it above all. The abundance of money is painted in a very false and empty way. The richest character in the book lives in a house completely void of colour, knowing if someone approaches her it's because of her bank account or for sex.<br /><br />The story also deals with fate - I mean, what are the chances that anyone would survive this crash? And what are the chances that one of them would be a painter who is obsessed with disasters, including plane crashes. And that this painter's childhood hero was Jack Lalanne, who swam to Alcatraz, dragging a boat behind him, inspiring him to join the swim team. What are the chances that he would find the boy, and because of his body's determination, find the shore? What does fate have in store for him after the crash? How will his life look after this incredible fall?<br /><br />This was much more than a "page-turner". I look forward to seeing what Noah Hawley writes next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3014626217933837632" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dem" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dem" href="/user/show/2752994-dem">Dem</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2857286182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7435545168940087076"><<br/><b>An enjoyable, well written and engaging novel by the author of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12246894.The_Good_Father' title='The Good Father by Noah Hawley' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Good Father</a>. Noah Hawley gets characterization and the construction of a tight and suspenseful plot.</b><br/><br/>A private plane crash on its way back from Martha’s Vineyard, a man and a small boy survive out of the eleven passengers on board and so the media circus begins and the search for answers.<br/><br/>The story is told from multiple viewpoints which works really well and keeps the story fresh and entertaining. The media coverage of the events</span>
  <span id="freeText7435545168940087076" style="display:none">&lt;<br /><b>An enjoyable, well written and engaging novel by the author of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12246894.The_Good_Father" title="The Good Father by Noah Hawley" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Good Father</a>. Noah Hawley gets characterization and the construction of a tight and suspenseful plot.</b><br /><br />A private plane crash on its way back from Martha’s Vineyard, a man and a small boy survive out of the eleven passengers on board and so the media circus begins and the search for answers.<br /><br />The story is told from multiple viewpoints which works really well and keeps the story fresh and entertaining. The media coverage of the events after the Fall was scarily reflective of the way reporting of stories and news has been sensationalized over the past few years. Now I find over hyped and sensational reporting to be pretty much the norm. What happened to reporting the facts or as a society are we just not interest in the facts anymore as fact are just too boring.<br /><br />As we we’ve through the passenger’s backstories we start to unravel the truth behind the crash and while this isn’t a fast-paced edge of your seat thriller it does a good job in keeping the reader’s attention right until the end.<br /><br />An enjoyable and thought-provoking thriller that would make a good book club discussion novel. Just to note I did start the audible version of this book but had to return as the narration was poor and took away from the enjoyment of the book for me.</span>

<div id="review_1660530517" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1660530517" />
    <a title="Susanne  Strong" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4514828-susanne-strong"><img alt="Susanne  Strong" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583087410p2/4514828.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1660530517?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susanne  Strong" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susanne  Strong" href="/user/show/4514828-susanne-strong">Susanne  Strong</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781455561780" href="/book/show/26245850-before-the-fall">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1660530517" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8809273479250878674">Well written, suspenseful and full of surprises. <br/><br/>Before the Fall is a book containing extremely rich (no pun intended) characters, most of whom are quite flawed; some are likeable (Scott, Eleanor & Gus), some are detestable (Bill & Doug, etc.). Throughout the book, everyone is trying to figure out who or what caused the crash, That is the mystery.. Who are the good guys? Are there good guys or is everyone so fatally flawed that it makes them sinister? Scott at first, is portrayed as the hero tho</span>
  <span id="freeText8809273479250878674" style="display:none">Well written, suspenseful and full of surprises. <br /><br />Before the Fall is a book containing extremely rich (no pun intended) characters, most of whom are quite flawed; some are likeable (Scott, Eleanor &amp; Gus), some are detestable (Bill &amp; Doug, etc.). Throughout the book, everyone is trying to figure out who or what caused the crash, That is the mystery.. Who are the good guys? Are there good guys or is everyone so fatally flawed that it makes them sinister? Scott at first, is portrayed as the hero though the media slowly tries to shatter that image, simply because, well, it makes for a better story. <br /><br />Several thought provoking issues are brought up, via the media coverage of the events after the Fall, that make me wonder: 1) How much of the news reported today is real and how much is trumped up?; and 2) How far do journalists really go to get the story? (I guess those questions could be answered by Brian Williams. :-))<br /><br />Noah Hawley did an excellent job of providing back stories for each of the characters. He then wove them together beautifully leading up to the events of the mysterious fall. The book's pace never slows keep the reader's interest until the end. <br /><br />In truth, it was an extremely satisfying read that I wished wouldn't have to end.. I wanted to follow Scott whenever he went, but what would that make me? A stalker or worse, the Paparazzi? Lol. :-)<br /><br />Published: June 8, 2016<br />Published on Goodreads and Amazon<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8809273479250878674" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1660530517">

<div id="review_1671914849" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1671914849" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1671914849?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781455561780" href="/book/show/26245850-before-the-fall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1671914849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5630428406760578851">A private jet carrying eleven people crashes into the ocean on its way from Martha's Vineyard to NYC. Against all odds, one of the passengers, Scott Burroughs, a fine art painter, survives the crash, finds the one other survivor, the four year old son of the executive who chartered the plane, and starts to swim ten miles to shore with the boy. <blockquote>Something brushes against his leg.<br/><br/>He freezes, starts to sink, then has to kick his legs to stay afloat.<br/><br/><i>Shark,</i> he thinks.<br/><br/><i>You have to stay still.</i><br/><br/>But if he s</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText5630428406760578851" style="display:none">A private jet carrying eleven people crashes into the ocean on its way from Martha's Vineyard to NYC. Against all odds, one of the passengers, Scott Burroughs, a fine art painter, survives the crash, finds the one other survivor, the four year old son of the executive who chartered the plane, and starts to swim ten miles to shore with the boy. <blockquote>Something brushes against his leg.<br /><br />He freezes, starts to sink, then has to kick his legs to stay afloat.<br /><br /><i>Shark,</i> he thinks.<br /><br /><i>You have to stay still.</i><br /><br />But if he stops moving he'll drown.<br /><br />He rolls over on his back, breathing deeply to inflate his chest. He has never been more aware of his tenuous place on the food chain.</blockquote>This push to survive against incredible odds is truly gripping.<br /><br />The rest of the novel repeatedly jumps from past to present and back again. There are flashbacks to the past as it explores the lives of each of the nine people who died in the crash: the executive of a conservative cable channel, his wife and nine year old daughter, their Israeli bodyguard, the money manager under an SEC investigation for money laundering, his wife, the crew. Hawley examines the the good and the ugly things in each of their lives, humanizing the tragedy of their loss. <br /><br />In between, we follow the aftermath of the crash, including its effects on the lives of Scott and the boy, JJ, those who care about them, and those who just want to use them, interspersed with detailed descriptions of Scott's disaster-themed series of paintings. There's also the official investigation and the search for the wrecked plane at the bottom of the ocean. The novel slowly works its way around to unfolding the mystery of why the crash happened, with a few red herrings along the way to make life interesting, along with some actual clues. <br /><br />I thought the final explanation of the reason for the crash was just a little anticlimactic, and I wasn't enamored with the subplot that involves a Fox News-like TV commentator, a horrible person who is the face of media frenzy, spinning news until it's not recognizable as news any longer. But these are fairly minor complaints.<br /><br />Even before the crash, Scott Burroughs is haunted by disasters, some of them caused by his own life choices.<blockquote>He was a disaster survivor in that he had survived the disaster that was his life. And so that's what he painted.</blockquote>Ultimately this is a novel about coping with whatever disasters life might bring, large or small, and being a survivor. It's a solid, tense novel and a compelling story, but it was the periodic flashes of insight that made it a memorable read for me.<br /><br /><i>I received a free copy of this ebook from Netgalley and the publisher in exchange for a review. Thank you!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5630428406760578851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer632443961925459930">This is a clear cut case of "it's not you, it's me." This book was not for me, please take my review with a grain of salt.<br/><br/>I was under the impression that this was a thriller/suspense novel, and I didn't get that vibe at all from this book. It was quite slow in parts, and though there is the mystery of the plane crash, I came to the point of not even caring what happened. <br/><br/>It is an interesting look at today's world of entertainment, and perception vs. reality.   <span id="freeText632443961925459930" style="display:none">This is a clear cut case of "it's not you, it's me." This book was not for me, please take my review with a grain of salt.<br /><br />I was under the impression that this was a thriller/suspense novel, and I didn't get that vibe at all from this book. It was quite slow in parts, and though there is the mystery of the plane crash, I came to the point of not even caring what happened. <br /><br />It is an interesting look at today's world of entertainment, and perception vs. reality. I also thought the format of the book was interesting, I enjoyed how the chapters were broken down into individual backgrounds, however I didn't enjoy the individual backgrounds themselves.<br /><br />All in all, I would give this book 2.5 stars rounded up.<br /><br />Thank you, Netgalley, for a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1684236547?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/1166663-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781455561780" href="/book/show/26245850-before-the-fall">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1684236547" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4705865153085081911">An entertaining summer read. <br/><br/><b>The Hook</b> A disaster and a hero. Can’t hurt that Author, Noah Hawley is creator of the TV Fargo.<br/><br/><b>The Line</b> <i>” How any two people end up in the same place at the same time is a mystery.”</i><br/><br/><b>The Sinker</b> – I loved the beginning pages of <u>Before the Fall</u>. Then I found myself losing interest only to regain the flow only to be disappointed in the end and wanting to make a noise like they do on Antique Roadshow when the value goes down. <br/><br/>Hype has raised it’s ugly head once again. Too </span>
  <span id="freeText4705865153085081911" style="display:none">An entertaining summer read. <br /><br /><b>The Hook</b> A disaster and a hero. Can’t hurt that Author, Noah Hawley is creator of the TV Fargo.<br /><br /><b>The Line</b> <i>” How any two people end up in the same place at the same time is a mystery.”</i><br /><br /><b>The Sinker</b> – I loved the beginning pages of <u>Before the Fall</u>. Then I found myself losing interest only to regain the flow only to be disappointed in the end and wanting to make a noise like they do on Antique Roadshow when the value goes down. <br /><br />Hype has raised it’s ugly head once again. Too many glowing reviews, too many promises claiming <u>Before the Fall</u> <i>”the thriller of the year”</i>.<br /><br />Eleven passengers board a private plane on Martha’s Vineyard. Ten were privileged, the last, a broke, would be artist, fasten their seat belts for the quick ride to New York. Disaster strikes, the plane crashes, the artist survives and miraculously saves the life of the four-year old son of the wealthy owner of the jet. These opening pages are the ones that kept me turning the pages. <br /><br />As you might expect the balance of the story is concerned with “what the heck happened?” and who or what was responsible for the crash. There are plenty of suspects and motive abounds. I enjoyed learning the back-stories of all who boarded the plane. To his credit Hawley formats the getting to the answers quite well even given the spoiler I am adding. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I saw the ending coming, almost from the beginning. It was ordinary as life often is. Perhaps this ordinariness was the author’s intent.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Well written, fast paced, good character development but not edge of the seat, hold your breath thrilling for me. Did I mention Jack LaLanne plays an important part in the telling? Now that part was excellent.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4705865153085081911" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1444886283" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1444886283" />
    <a title="Jan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15865336-jan"><img alt="Jan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468934637p2/15865336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1444886283?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jan" href="/user/show/15865336-jan">Jan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/27868408-before-the-fall">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15865336-jan?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15865336-jan?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1444886283" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13906669237318451551">4.5 stars<br/><br/>I have always been intrigued by plane crashes. More in the 'oh there's an accident, let me see what is going on' kind of fascination. So much mystery involved: Why did it crash-was it foul play or a mechanical issue? Did the passengers know what was happening? There are still many unanswered questions about some major plane crashes today, with teams of people and tons of money devoted to trying to find some answers.<br/><br/>This is a book about one such fictional plane crash, with a total of 11 </span>
  <span id="freeText13906669237318451551" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />I have always been intrigued by plane crashes. More in the 'oh there's an accident, let me see what is going on' kind of fascination. So much mystery involved: Why did it crash-was it foul play or a mechanical issue? Did the passengers know what was happening? There are still many unanswered questions about some major plane crashes today, with teams of people and tons of money devoted to trying to find some answers.<br /><br />This is a book about one such fictional plane crash, with a total of 11 on board and only 2 survivors. As the story unfolds, so does the drama. While this is no way suspenseful, it certainly provides a great mystery to solve. And unlike some of today's real life crashes, the author was kind enough to provide the reader with an answer to the mystery--one that I was completely satisfied with.<br /><br />Every character's past is dissected (both victim's and survivor's) weaving back and forth between their past and back into the present where a full scale investigation is ongoing and fingers are being pointed everywhere. I don't know how accurate all of the investigative parts are, but it sure was a fascinating look at the 'behind the scenes' of what can take place during an investigation.<br /><br />I highly recommend this well-constructed page turner. I haven't read anything like it before, and it was a breathe of fresh air!<br /><br />My thanks to NetGalley for the ARC in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13906669237318451551" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ivy+vZZjuUMrPgZPbTaReHCb6uTVn3b/cdm/EWODl8Wf/ixcBOIGr9/bZwB/6ClCgji60vQ6H8UUwekVCj4yCA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vtQu0J67EkjYXF9NnTMvlmCC4fGP+UyOtWJLce3YTxOr1rwxDDqtpCy5PgKP7ZeskiGxx65cJbTQeh11hGXq3g==')})
  }

A series of wrong turns and disastrous life choices has led to their incarceration. Following their release, Mangle, Decker and Tazeem stick together as they return to a life of crime, embarking on a lucrative scam. But when they stumble upon a sophisticated sex-trafficking operation, they soon realise that they are in mortal danger. The disappearance of a family member and the murder of a dear friend lead the three to delve deeper into a world of violence and deception. In their quest for retribution and justice, they put their lives on the line. Their paths cross with that of Tatiana, who has left her home country for a better life in the West—or so she thinks. She soon realises she is in the hands of ruthless, violent people, who run an operation supplying girls to meet the most deviant desires of rich and powerful men. He has published four novels and penned the script for the feature film Lies and Alibis.   <span id="freeText6070283526788531538" style="display:none">Noah Hawley is an Emmy, Golden Globe, PEN, Critics' Choice, and Peabody Award-winning author, screenwriter, and producer. He has published four novels and penned the script for the feature film Lies and Alibis. He created, executive produced, and served as showrunner for ABC's My Generation and The Unusuals and was a writer and producer on the hit series Bones. Hawley is currently executive producer, writer, and showrunner on FX's award-winning series, Fargo.</span>
